Commerce Parkway
                                                                                 ii
SECTION 1 ­ GENERAL PROJECT INFORMATION

1.1 STUDY OBJECTIVE

The objective of this document is to provide Florida Department of Transportation (FDOT) with
Design Traffic volumes for the proposed alignment of Commerce Parkway from US 1 to SR 100
(Moody Boulevard) in Flagler County, Florida. The scope of this Technical Memorandum entails
the development of future traffic forecasts and basic operational conditions of the corridor during
the design life of the project.

1.2 METHODOLOGY

The methodology and development of Design Traffic is consistent with the Design Traffic
Handbook (Topic No. 525-030-120-g) published by FDOT. The methodology covers the
following topics:

           Collect available traffic count information from FDOT historical traffic count records
           and from actual field count data, review of previous studies, traffic characteristics,
           and other relevant data.
           Estimate future travel characteristics for the corridor based on data collected within
           the project area. This includes Design Hour Factor (K30), Design Hour Directional
           Factor (D30), and Design Truck Factor (Tdaily).
           Develop estimates of future traffic volumes using historical traffic counts obtained
           from FDOT count stations within the study area (Trends Analysis), historic growth
           rates, statistical (population and economic growth projections) and/or adopted travel
           demand models (FSUTMS) for the area.
           Evaluate the future volumes based on capacity to determine whether the corridor will
           operate under constrained or unconstrained conditions.
           Modify travel characteristics (K-demand) based on constrained or unconstrained
           conditions.
           Develop Opening Year, Mid-Design Year, and Design Year traffic projections for the
           project.
           Provide a Level of Service (LOS) analysis for the corridor.

1.3 PROJECT LOCATION AND LIMITS

The project limits along US 1 extend from south of the intersection of US 1 and Belle Terre
Boulevard to north of the intersection of US 1 and SR 100/ SR 11. The project limits include SR
100 (Moody Boulevard) from east of the intersection of SR 100 and Belle Terre Boulevard to
west of the intersection of SR 100/SR 11 and US 1/ South Street. The segment of Belle Terre
Boulevard from the intersection of US 1 and Belle Terre Boulevard to the intersection of SR 100
and Belle Terre Boulevard is also included in the project limits.




Traffic Technical Memorandum                                                      February 2012
Commerce Parkway
                                                1
The study corridor includes the following three signalized intersections:

     SR 100 (Moody Boulevard) at Belle Terre Boulevard
     SR 100 / SR 11 at US 1/ South Street
     US 1 at Belle Terre Boulevard

roadway network.

SECTION 2 - PROJECT INFORMATION & DATA COLLECTION

2.1 Data Collection

Information for the study area was obtained from Flagler County, FDOT and other available data
resources. The most recent version of the Central Florida Regional Planning Model (CFRPM
v4.50) was obtained from FDOT.

Traffic counts were collected from November 30 to December 2, 2010. Table 1 summarizes
traffic count locations, type of counts and date of counts.

                               Table 1 ­ Traffic Count Locations

        Count Location                   Type of Counts                     Date of Count

   Boulevard and SR 100                       counts                          12/2/2010

The classification counts consisted of the following three vehicle classifications:

         Passenger Vehicles (Class 1 through 3) ­ motorcycles, cars, vans, pickups;
         Light Trucks (FHWA Vehicle Class 4 through 13) ­ buses and 2-axle, single unit
         trucks, single trailer
         Heavy Trucks (FHWA Vehicle Class 4, 5, and 6 axles) and two or more trailers (5, 6,
         and 7 axles)

Based on these categories, percentages for overall trucks were determined for peak and daily
traffic conditions.

The 72-hour vehicle counts were adjusted to annual average daily traffic (AADT) based on the
most current FDOT seasonal adjustment factor of 1.07 and axle factor of 0.94. The vehicle
classification counts were adjusted to AADT based on the seasonal adjustment factor of 1.07.

Four-hour turning movement counts (TMC) were collected on November 4, 2010 during the a.m.
and p.m. peak periods (7:00 to 9:00 a.m. and 4:00 to 6:00 p.m. respectively) to determine turning
movement volumes at the signalized intersections.

TMC were adjusted using the seasonal adjustment factor of 1.03.
Turning movement counts were collected at the following three intersections:

      SR 100 (Moody Boulevard) at Belle Terre Boulevard
      SR 100 / SR 11 at US 1/ South Street
      US 1 at Belle Terre Boulevard

The traffic count data are provided in Appendix A of this Technical Memorandum.

2.2 Design Characteristics

Existing traffic characteristics for the project corridor, including the design hour factor (K30),
directional distribution factor (D30) and daily truck factor (Tdaily), were developed from the 72-
hour vehicle counts collected as part of this study. Existing travel characteristics from the FDOT
Roadway Characteristics Inventory (RCI) for FDOT count stations on state roads in the project
area were also obtained for comparison with the measured traffic characteristics. The measured
design characteristics values for K, D and T are shown in Table 2.

Based on the measured peak to daily ratio, an estimated value of K30 (design hour demand for the
30th highest hour) was developed based on the ratio of the median seasonal factor for the highest
13 weeks (peak season) and the median seasonal factor for the lowest 13 weeks (non-peak
season). For this study, an adjustment factor of 1.11 was used for the corridor. The Peak Season
Factor Category Report is provided in Appendix B.


Traffic Technical Memorandum                                                     February 2012
Commerce Parkway
                                                4
As shown in Table 2, the estimated K30 value for the roadways in the project area ranged from
9.15 percent to 10.91 percent with an average of 9.96 percent. This number is very close to the
reported K value at the FDOT count stations within the project area. Commerce Parkway will be
classified as a suburban arterial within the project limits. Highway Capacity Manual (HCM)
national averages indicate a minimum of 10.0 percent for a suburban arterial. The FDOT
recommended K30 values for urban arterial ranges from 9.2 to 11.5 with an average of 10.2.
Therefore, the recommended future K30 value for this study is 10.15 percent.

The measured D ranged from 52.1 percent to 58.3 percent with an average of 55.8 percent. The
FDOT count stations within the area of study showed an estimated D30 of 58.2%. This FDOT
estimated D30 value is close to the measured D. The FDOT recommended D30 values for urban
arterial ranges from 50.8 to 67.1 with an average of 57.9. Therefore, the recommended D30
value for this study is 58.2 percent.

The measured daily truck percentage obtained from the classification count data ranged from 6.8
percent to 11.5 percent. The FDOT count stations within the area of study showed an estimated
Tdaily of 9.2 percent within the area. Since the average measured Tdaily is nearly identical to that
measured by the FDOT count stations, the recommended Tdaily for this study is 9.2%. The
estimated Tpeak value is 4.6%.




Traffic Technical Memorandum                                                       February 2012
Commerce Parkway
                                                 5
SECTION 3 - TRAFFIC FORECASTING

The development of traffic projections for Commerce Parkway involved the examination of
historical traffic growth and proposed development within the corridor vicinity in order to
comprehend a basic understanding of the traffic circulation patterns and characteristics of the
corridor.

3.1 Trends Analysis

Historical traffic count information was obtained from FDOT. Trend analyses were performed
based on the count stations within the project vicinity. There are seven FDOT count stations in
the general vicinity of the project. All historic count data were used to evaluate future traffic
growth in the project corridor that is statistically significant. The historical count data showed
significant fluctuations in traffic volumes from 1994 to 2009.

Future growth trends were established from the available data using a least square linear
regression of historic counts. The data from five of the seven count stations have an R2 value (a
statistical measure of how well a regression line approximates real data points) greater than 75%,
which is the minimum R2 considered acceptable. Table 3 presents the trend analysis results for
the FDOT count stations. Appendix C includes the trend analysis sheets for the count stations.
As seen in the table, the trend analysis shows a slight growth rate over the analysis period.

                       Table 3 - FDOT Count Station Historical Trends

                                                                                      Squared

  0013     SR 5, 0.03 Mi S of SR 20/100 Overpass                           1.82%       34.03%
  0033     SR 100, 0.159 Mi NE of SR 5                                     1.88%       76.56%

3.2 Central Florida Regional Planning Model

In addition to the historical traffic count based trends analysis, evaluation of traffic growth was
performed using the approved CFRPM 4.5 provided by FDOT. The CFRPM 4.5 model has a
base year 2000 and a long-range forecasting for the future year 2025. The modeling efforts used
the latest available socio-economic traffic analysis zone input (i.e., ZDATA) for a long-range
forecasting future year 2035. These ZDATA include projections of single and multi-family
dwelling units; service, industrial and commercial employment; and school enrollments. CFRPM
uses these input values to predict trip productions and trip attractions between the Traffic
Analysis Zones (TAZs).
Traffic Technical Memorandum                                                        February 2012
Commerce Parkway
                                                   6
There are four Development of Regional Impact studies (DRIs) ongoing in this area of Flagler
County (Old Brick Township, Town Center at Palm Coast, Plantation Bay, Neoga Lakes, and
Flagler Central Commerce Park) that are not included in the CFRPM 4.5 (see Figure 2). The
CFRPM model zonal structure was modified to include the TAZ's representing all four pending
DRIs. The socio-economic data in ZDATA 1 and ZDATA 2 files for Year 2035 were updated to
include the proposed land use for the four DRIs and the Flagler Central Commerce Park
development. The Flagler Central Commerce Park development abuts the proposed Commerce
Parkway.

                                Figure 2 - DRIs/SUB DRIs




Although both Old Brick Township and Neoga Lakes DRI's are not currently approved, they
were included in the model to estimate a more conservative trip distribution pattern and to
quantify the potential impacts of traffic generated by these DRIs on Commerce Parkway. Model
plots showing the number of lanes and Year 2035 model volumes with and without Commerce
Parkway are documented in Appendix D.

The model volumes were adjusted to determine the projected AADT along Commerce Parkway
using a Model Output Conversion Factor (MOCF) of 0.94. A simple linear growth projection
was calculated between the Year 2000 and Year 2035 model volumes. Table 3 summarizes the
calculated linear growth for those locations.

3.3 Socioeconomic Data

Future travel demand was also estimated based on land use data. The updated 2005 and 2035
land use data provided in the CFRPM model were examined to determine changes in land use
within the project area. Table 6 shows the growth rate calculation for the land use data for
selected Traffic Analysis Zones (TAZ) within the project area. Two TAZs were added for the
Flagler Central Commerce Park. TAZ 1797 represents the multi-family portion with the
population to dwelling unit ratio assumed from the parent TAZ and TAZ 1798 represents the
industrial and commercial portion of this development. The Flagler Central Commerce Park was
projected based upon external trips estimated using the Institute of Transportation Engineers Trip
Traffic Technical Memorandum                                                     February 2012
Commerce Parkway
                                                8
Generation Handbook, 7th edition as documented in Appendix E. At build out, the Flagler
Central Commerce Park is anticipated to generate approximately 14,500 daily external trips. The
land use analysis indicates that between Year 2000 and Year 2035 there is an average increase of
5.95% in the populations of single-family and multi-family residences and an increase of 6.79%
in the total employment within the vicinity of Commerce Parkway.

The results of the transportation model for this study area and the land use growth within the area
were reviewed to determine an appropriate average annual growth rate that reflects the
characteristics of the corridor. After discussion with FDOT District Five Office to use a
reasonable annual growth rate reflecting the area growth documented in Appendix F, an average
growth rate of 4.4% was accepted by the District Five Office as documented in Appendix F to
estimate the growth between the Existing Year (2010) and the Design Year (2035) for this study.

3.4 Design Traffic Forecasts

Forecasted AADT for the Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year (2025) and Design Year (2035) for
existing roadways within the project area were calculated by extrapolating the existing 2010
daily volumes to the year 2035 using the 4.4% average annual growth to project the future traffic
demand. The non-project traffic (i.e. not the Flagler Central Commerce Park development

Traffic Technical Memorandum                                                      February 2012
Commerce Parkway
                                                 9
project) along Commerce Parkway was assumed in 2035 by reassigning 12% or 2,300 daily
vehicles of the right turn volumes from US 1 to Belle Terre Parkway and its reciprocal
westbound SR 100 left-turn to southbound US 1 right-turn movement to Commerce Parkway.
For the opening year and mid-year diverted traffic from the US 1/SR 100 intersection to
Commerce Parkway is based upon a linear interpolation.

Based on the aforementioned design characteristics, Design Hour Volumes (DHV's) were
developed from the daily traffic forecasts. Due to the varying nature of peak and off-peak
directions associated with the intersections within the project corridor, specific intersection
turning movements for Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year (2025) and Design Year (2035) were
estimated to evaluate the projected traffic operations in the corridor. Future year turning
movement volumes were adjusted based on projected AADT estimates and resulted in the
projected annual growth rates by movement to fluctuate to balance the turning movement
volumes. The project intersection turning movement volumes are based upon the recommended
K30 and D30.

3.5 Level of Service Analysis

Operating conditions, expressed as level of service (LOS), are generally determined based on the
comparison between traffic volumes and roadway capacity. LOS analyses were performed for
the existing conditions and Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year (2025) and Design Year (2035) No-
Build and Build scenarios. The FDOT Level of Service Standard for Commerce Parkway is LOS
D.

Operational analyses were performed using the current adopted procedures as outlined in the
Highway Capacity Manual, Transportation Research Board, Special Report 209, 2000 (HCM).
Analyses were conducted for the signalized intersections as well as the arterial. Intersection
signal timings were optimized using SYNCHRO v7.0 for future conditions.

3.5.1 Existing Conditions

The existing lane configuration for the roadway network and the existing intersection
configurations are shown in Figure 3. The existing balanced turning movement volumes and
existing intersection and arterial levels of service are shown in Figure 4. The analyses were
conducted using the existing signal timings obtained from the City of Palm Coast and FDOT.
Table 7 presents the results of the intersection analyses. As seen in the table, all of the
intersections are currently operating at acceptable levels of service during both the a.m. and p.m.
peak hours with the exception of the unsignalized intersection at US 1 at Belle Terre Boulevard
that operates at LOS "F" in the a.m. peak hour.

 3.5.2 Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year (2025) and Design Year (2035) Analysis

 Both arterial and intersection analyses were conducted for Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year and
 Design Year (2035) conditions for the No-Build and Build Conditions. The following
 summarizes each of these analyses.

 Future Arterial Analysis

 Arterial analyses were performed using HIGHPLAN for Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year (2025)
 and Design Year (2035) for both the Build and No-Build conditions. Tables 8, 9 and 10
 summarize the HIGHPLAN LOS results for the Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year (2025) and the
 Design Year (2035), respectively. Commerce Parkway is projected to operate at LOS B or
 better in the Opening Year (2015), Mid-Year (2025) and the Design Year (2035). An
 HIGHPLAN analysis was not conducted in 2015 since Commerce Parkway is not anticipated to
 include any signalized intersections. Appendix G provides HIGHPLAN LOS output results for
 the roadway segments analyzed.

In the Mid-Year (2025), the US 1/Belle Terre Boulevard and the SR 100/Commerce Parkway
intersections were evaluated as signalized intersections since these intersections are anticipated
to operate at unacceptable levels of service in 2015. The US 1/SR 100 and the SR 100/Belle
Terre Boulevard intersections are anticipated to operate at LOS E and LOS F, respectively. With
the introduction of signalization to the US 1/Belle Terre Boulevard and SR 100/Commerce

Traffic Technical Memorandum                                                          February 2012
Commerce Parkway
                                                       14
Parkway intersections, those intersections are anticipated to operate at acceptable levels of
service. By the Mid-Year (2025), it is anticipated that the unsignalized intersection of
Commerce Parkway and US-1 will fail and operate at LOS F during both a.m. and p.m. peak
hours.

anticipated to operate at LOS B or better with signalization. The US 1/SR 100 and SR 100/Belle

improvements with or without Commerce Parkway. Signalization of Commerce Parkway at US
1 and SR 100 is assumed (subject to traffic signal warrants). The capacity analysis calculations
for the three future years are documented in Appendix H.

Commerce Parkway
                                        22
   SECTION 4 - CONCLUSIONS

This traffic report describes the process of determining the future year traffic projections after
construction of Commerce Parkway between US 1 and SR 100. As part of this process, both
existing and future traffic conditions were analyzed for US 1 from Belle Terre Parkway to SR
100, SR 100 from US 1/SR 11 to Belle Terre Parkway and Belle Terre Parkway from US 1 to SR
100. Existing intersections within the project area are projected to operate at LOS E or LOS F by
the Mid- Year (2025) without improvements. The analyses indicate a two-lane (one lane per
direction) roadway with separate turn lanes along Commerce Parkway is projected to operate at
LOS B or better through the Design Year (2035). In 2025, it is anticipated that the SR
100/Commerce Parkway intersection may require signalization, subject to traffic warrants. By
2035, the US 1/Commerce Parkway is anticipated to require signalization, subject to a traffic
warrant study.

FDOT ­ District Five Correspondence
March 9, 2011
To: Terry Rains, Jon Weiss - FDOT
From: Bob Johnson, Chris Rizzolo ­ URS

RE: Commerce Parkway ­ Existing Conditions and 2035 CFRPM Build/No-Build
Model Runs and Growth Trend Summary

This memorandum documents existing conditions and the Central Florida Regional
Planning Model (CFRPM) model runs for the proposed Commerce Parkway to assist the
Department in review of the model runs used to develop annual growth rates for future
traffic projections. These model runs include the Flagler Central Commerce Park
development. Commerce Parkway was added to the "Build" CFRPM based upon the
Flagler Central Commerce Park site plan.

PROJECT INFORMATION & DATA COLLECTION

Data Collection

Information for the study area was obtained from Flagler County, FDOT and other
available data resources. The most recent version of the Central Florida Regional
Planning Model (CFRPM v4.50) was obtained from FDOT.

Traffic counts were collected the weeks of November 3 and November 29, 2010. Traffic
counts included three 48-hour vehicle counts: one on SR 11 west of US 1, one on US 1
south of Belle Terre Boulevard and one on Belle Terre Boulevard between US 1 and SR
100. Three 72-hour vehicle classification counts included one on US 1 north of SR 100,
one on SR 100 between US 1 and Belle Terre Boulevard and one on US 1 between Belle
Terre Boulevard and SR 100. The classification counts consisted of the following three
vehicle classifications:

         Passenger Vehicles (Class 1 through 3) ­ motorcycles, cars, vans, pickups;
         Trucks (Class 4 through 13) ­ buses and 2-axle, single unit trucks, single trailer
         (4, 5, and 6 axles) and two or more trailers (5, 6, and 7 axles)

Based on these categories, percentages for overall trucks were determined for peak and
daily traffic conditions.

The 48-hour vehicle counts were adjusted to annual average daily traffic (AADT) based
on the most current FDOT seasonal adjustment factor of 1.07 and axle factor of 0.94. The
vehicle classification counts were adjusted to AADT based on the seasonal adjustment
factor of 1.07.

Four-hour turning movement counts (TMC) were collected on November 4, 2010 during
the a.m. and p.m. peak periods to determine turning movement volumes at the signalized

                                            1
  intersections. Turning movement counts were collected at the following three
  intersections:

                        SR 100 (Moody Boulevard) at Belle Terre Boulevard
                        SR 100 / SR 11 at US 1/ South Street
                        US 1 at Belle Terre Boulevard

  The traffic count data are provided in Appendix A.

  Design Characteristics

  Existing traffic characteristics for the project corridor, including the design hour factor
  (K30), directional distribution factor (D30) and daily truck factor (Tdaily), were developed
  from the 48-hour vehicle counts collected as part of this study. Existing travel
  characteristics from the FDOT Roadway Characteristics Inventory (RCI) for FDOT count
  stations on state roads in the project area were also obtained for comparison with the
  measured traffic characteristics. The recommended design characteristics values for K, D
  and T are shown in Table 1.

                      Table 1 - Recommended Design Traffic Characteristics

                        Location                                   K           D          T
SR 100 West of Belle Terre Pkwy                                  9.89*      56.8%*      6.8%*

                                 Location                          K           D          T

730013      SR 5, 0.03 Mi S of SR 20/100 Overpass                10.15       58.2%       7.2%
730054      SR 100, 1.94 Mi NE of SR 5                           10.15       58.2%       9.2%

  Based on the measured peak to daily ratio, an estimated value of K30 (design hour
  demand for the 30th highest hour) was developed based on the ratio of the median
  seasonal factor for the highest 13 weeks (peak season) and the median seasonal factor for
  the lowest 13 weeks (non-peak season). For this study, an adjustment factor of 1.11 was
  used for the corridor.


                                               2
   As shown in Table 1, the measured peak to daily ratio for the roadways in the project area
   ranged from 9.15 percent to 10.91 percent with an average of 9.96 percent. This number
   is very close to the reported K value at the FDOT count stations within the project area.
   Commerce Parkway will be classified as a suburban arterial within the project limits.
   Highway Capacity Manual (HCM) national averages indicate a minimum of 10.0 percent
   for a suburban arterial. Therefore, the recommended future K30 value for this study is
   10.2 percent.

   The measured D ranged from 52.1 percent to 58.3 percent with an average of 55.8
   percent. The FDOT count stations within the area of study showed an estimated D30 of
   58.2%. This FDOT estimated D30 value is close to the measured D. Therefore, the
   recommended D30 value for this study is 58.2 percent.

   The measured daily truck percentage obtained from the classification count data ranged
   from 6.8 percent to 11.5 percent. The FDOT count stations within the area of study
   showed an estimated Tdaily of 9.2 percent within the area. Since the average measured
   Tdaily is nearly identical to that measured by the FDOT count stations, the recommended
   Tdaily for this study is 9.2%. The estimated Tpeak value is 4.6%.

   Existing Conditions

   The existing lane configuration for the roadway network and the existing intersection
   configurations are shown in Figure 1. The existing turning movement counts and existing
   intersection and arterial levels of service are shown in Figure 2. The analyses were
   conducted using the existing signal timings obtained from the City of Palm Coast and
   FDOT. Table 2 presents the results of the intersection analyses. As seen in the table, all
   of the intersections are currently operating at acceptable levels of service during both the
   a.m. and p.m. peak hours with the exception of SR 100 at Belle Terre Boulevard, which
   is operating at LOS E in the a.m. peak hour.

                          5
CFRPM MODEL RUNS

The Flagler Central Commerce Park development (see Figure 3) is anticipated to generate
approximately 14,500 daily external trips for the 300 multi-family DU's, 700,000 sq. ft.
of light industrial, and 200,000 sq. ft. of commercial. The 14,500 daily trips is based
upon Institute of Transportation Engineers' Trip Generation, 8th Edition rates, where
approximately 11% of the gross trips are internally captured and 10% of the commercial
development is attributable to pass-by capture trips. The pass-by capture trips were
determined from the 2035 AADT traffic without the Flagler Central Commerce Park
development. The Flagler Central Commerce Park development trip generation
characteristics, together with an update to the CFRPM model growth calculations, are
summarized in Table 3. A CFRPM model run that does not include the Flagler Central
Commerce Park development is documented in Figure 4. Along SR 100, it is assumed
that 10% of the 18,600 daily background traffic (i.e. without the Flagler Central
Commerce Park development) is attributable to pass-by capture trips to/from the
commercial development.

    Table 3 ­ Central Commerce Park Development Trip Generation Summary
 Time of Day   Gross Trips    Internal Trips    Pass-By Capture Trips    External Trips
Daily          17,725         1,378            1,860                    14,487

Surrounding DRIs & Sub-DRI Socio Economic Changes

Two TAZs were added for the Flagler Central Commerce Park. TAZ 1797 represents the
multi-family portion and TAZ 1798 represents the industrial and commercial portion of
this development. There are four Development of Regional Impact studies (DRIs)
ongoing in this area of Flagler County (Old Brick Township, Town Center at Palm Coast,
Plantation Bay, and Neoga Lakes) that are not included in the CFRPM 4.5. The location
of the surrounding DRI's and sub-DRI's are illustrated in Figure 5. The socio-economic
data in ZDATA 1 and ZDATA 2 files for Year 2035 were updated to include the
proposed land use for the four DRIs. The Traffic Analysis Zones (TAZs) for the Flagler
Central Commerce Park development and the surrounding DRI's are summarized in
Table 4.

FDOT Historical Trend & CFRPM Trend Comparison

The growth trend was updated for the Flagler Central Commerce Park development from the
2035 CFRPM Build model run. Table 6 summarizes the five roadways' annual growth
percentages results from a based year (2000) model and the future (2035) model run. The
FDOT trend analyses for these five road segments are documented in Appendix B.

The results of the transportation model for this study area and the land use projections
within the area were reviewed to determine an appropriate average annual growth that
reflects the characteristics of the corridor. An average annual growth of 4.4% is proposed
to estimate the growth between the existing (2010) year, opening (2015) year, interim
(2025) year, and the design (2035) year for this study.




                                             11
          Table 6 ­ CFRPM Version 4.5 Model Linear Growth Calculation




Next, the CFRPM Version 4.5 model was compared with the FDOT Trend analysis based
upon historical traffic counts for the same five roadways. The three trend analyses along
with an average of these trends are summarized in Table 7.

A 4.4% annual growth is recommended along US 1, SR 100, and Belle Terre Boulevard
located south of SR 100. If a 4.4% annual growth is assumed along Belle Terre
Boulevard north of SR 100, then 35,400 AADT vehicles would be anticipated which is
greater than the CFRPM model projection of 20,900 AADT vehicles. Except at the
northeast corner of SR 100/Belle Terre Boulevard intersection, the adjacent land located
north of SR 100 along Belle Terre Boulevard is already developed. Since the available
counts along Belle Terre Boulevard located north of SR 100 results in a low R square
value and this count was not used to derive the 4.4% annual growth, we suggest using the
CFRPM model volume of 20,900 for the year 2035. The opening and interim years for
this roadway would be interpolated from the existing counts and the 2035 AADT.
                                            12
                   Table 7 ­ Commerce Parkway Trend Analyses




Commerce Parkway Traffic Diversion

On average, approximately 19% of the traffic is anticipated to be diverted from the
northbound US 1 to eastbound SR 100 right-turn and its reciprocal westbound to
southbound left-turn at the US 1/SR 100 intersection. This was determined from a trace
of the US 1 traffic located south of the proposed Commerce Parkway and a trace of the
SR 100 traffic located east of the proposed Commerce Parkway. The US 1 and SR 100
trace is attached in Appendix C. Without Commerce Parkway, the traffic diverted from
US 1 and SR 100 will continue to arrive at the US 1 and SR 100 intersection in a No-
Build scenario.




                                         13
Memorandum
Prepared For: Florida Department of Transportation District 5 Planning
To:              Terry Rains, Project Manager-Design Traffic, FDOT D5
Prepared By: Veena Madineni, P.E., Ghyabi & Associates
Date:            March 15, 2011
Re:   Commerce Parkway ­ Existing Conditions and 2035 CFRPM Build/No-Build
Model Runs and Growth Trend Summary


Ghyabi & Associates, Inc. (G&A) has analyzed the Commerce Parkway ­ Existing Conditions
and 2035 CFRPM Build/No-Build Model Runs and Growth Trend Summary Memorandum
dated March 9, 2011. This memorandum for Commerce Parkway has summarized the data
collection performed for this study, developed design traffic characteristics, evaluated existing
operating conditions and established future growth rates using CFRPM Model and historic
trends. Our comments of this initial review are presented below:

      A. Please include a table and/or a graphic with AADTs from the counts. Appendix A lists
         ADTs and applying a SF of 1.07 does not match with numbers provided in Figure 2. For
         example, for US 1 north of Belle Terre Blvd. gives an AADT of 11,100 whereas Figure 2
         lists it as 10,500. Also in Figure 2, the legend is incorrect for text in red [AM (PM)
         DDHV].
      B. In Figure 1, the geometry for SR 100 at Belle Terre Blvd. is incorrect. SB movement
         includes dual left turn lanes. Also, SR 100 is a 4 lane section for the most part, but it
         tapers down to a 2 lane section as it approaches US 1 to the west.
      C. Turning Movement Counts for US 1 and SR 100/Moody Blvd. intersection are not
         included in the Appendices. Also, the HCS analysis summary sheets for intersections
         need to be included for verification.
      D. The scope lists QLOS to be performed for Arterial which is not included in the attached
         memorandum.
      E. The trip generation and internal capture rates for the daily conditions have been verified.
         Also, since a peak hour analysis will be done for the study, trip generation estimations for
         the peak hour are also needed to cross-check the peak hour volume.
      F. Also, please note that the pass-by trips typically limited to not exceed 10% of the
         roadway demand. So, depending on the final growth rate for SR 100 a check has to be
         made against the % pass-by trips.



                                                                                            P a g e  1 
 
    G. Page 6, the memo lists that four DRIs (Old Brick Township, Town Center at Palm Coast,
       Plantation Bay, and Neoga Lakes) have been added to the base zdata. Table 1 lists zdata
       for developments within the vicinity of the project, but this list does not include
       information for Old Brick Township, Plantation Bay and Neoga Lakes. Any changes
       made to the zdata and/or network need to be listed in the memorandum.
    H. In Table 4, it is surprising that the zdata for TAZ 3616, representing the DRI Town
       Center at Palm Coast has such low employment by 2035. This TAZ represents Palm
       Coast High School, Florida Hospital and has retail services in it.
    I. Also in Table 4, the occupancy rate (Pop/D.U.) used for the Flagler Commerce Park
       development (TAZ 1797) is high for a Multi-Family Dwelling Units. This rate is higher
       than those used for Single Family units.
    J. Page 10 (Figures 6 & 7), the Centroid connections for 1797 representing the Residential
       units are not consistent. On the first one, it loads to SR 100 and in the second, it is
       centered to the south end of Commerce Parkway. For true comparison, the centroid
       connections have to be consistent.
    K. Page 12, Table 6 lists the growth rates from the model (2000 to 2035), Count to model
       data and historic trends.
           i. It is observed that the year 2000 AADT (from model) is a lot lower than the actual
              counts for those locations. For example, Locations 1 and 2 have a recorded AADT
              of 10,500 and 10,800 whereas the model AADT is 6,000 and 5,100, respectively.
              The total AADT for five locations is 45,800 from counts vs. 32,900 as obtained
              from the model. CFRPM is a regional validated model; however, careful review is
              necessary when using it for a sub-area analysis such as this. The average growth
              rate of 6.31% from the model is significantly high.
          ii. In the second part of Table 6, the 2009 AADTs listed for locations 3 and 4 are
              incorrect. The numbers seem to be flipped.
    L. Please include R2 values in Table 7, so the reliability of the growth rates from trends can
       be established. Also, the FDOT's Project Traffic Forecasting Handbook recommends
       using current plus nine earlier years of historical traffic count data for projecting traffic
       growth, whereas in this case, counts dated back to 1994 have been used. Please document
       your reasoning for using data beyond a 10 year period.
    M. Considering the significantly high growth from the historic counts and also the model, a
       review of the historic trends at decaying exponential rate and BEBR population
       projections for the area would also help.
    N. Also, the memo does not specify if Flagler Central Commerce Park development is
       phased. If true, then one growth rate is not applicable for the interim years.


                                                                                           P a g e  2 
 
    O. Page 12, second paragraph includes a discussion on the growth rate for Belle Terre
       Parkway located north of SR 100. Please mention 2010 AADT, so a comparison can be
       made against the recommended 2035 AADT obtained from the model. Traffic count
       report published by the city of Palm Coast lists 2008 daily volume for Belle Terre
       Parkway from East Hampton Boulevard to SR 100 as 22,485. Taking into consideration
       that the section of Belle Terre Parkway north of Town Center is fairly built-up, a smaller
       growth rate may be assumed for future projections.
    P. Page 13, the following statement is misleading: "Without Commerce Parkway, the traffic
       diverted from US 1 and SR 100 will continue to arrive at the US 1 and SR 100
       intersection in a No-Build scenario".

       From the select link model runs, the traffic from northbound U.S. 1 or westbound S.R.
       100 is not through traffic, these volumes are related to Flagler Central Commerce Park
       development (TAZ 1797 and 1798) only, and travel characteristics of these trips will
       depend on the site access/ centroid connectors. In order to estimate true diversion, site
       access to the development in No-Build condition needs to be established. For example, if
       the site only has access to SR 100, then diversion for northbound US 1 to eastbound
       Commerce Parkway and the return movement is valid, but diversion for traffic movement
       from westbound SR 100 to Commerce Parkway will not exist as this traffic will enter the
       development before getting to S.R. 100 and U.S. 1 intersection. A select link analysis for
       No-Build condition may be necessary to establish diversion.
